CHAPTER 5 .
An Act to amend the Explosives Act ,1875 ,in its
applicationto Northern Ireland.
[27th May ,1924.]

thereof-
" (11)A person under the age of eighteenyears

sixteen years shallnot be employed in any such

the principalAct relatingtheretoshallhave effectaccord-

ofthe Towns Improvement (Ireland) Act, 1854,

a-bancs. [29th May , 1924.]
BEE itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1.-(1) The provisionsof the Towns Improvement(Ireland) Act , 1854, (in this Act referredto as " the
principalAct ") with respectto hackney carriagesshall,
notwithstandinganything contained in sectionseventy-
eightof the principalAct,apply to every char-a-banc as
definedinthissection;and referencestohackney carriages,
hackney coaches, or carriagesand to driversthereof,
whenever they occur in any of the saidprovisions, shall
be deemed to includereferencesto every such char-a-banc
and the driver and conductor thereof :
Provided that,in the case of any char-a-banc used
solelyfor the carriageof passengersfrom places within
the prescribeddistanceto and from places outsidethe
prescribeddistance, such of the aforesaidprovisionsof
the principalAct as arespecifiedin the Schedule to this
Act shallnot apply.

plying or standingforhireorused to carry passengersat
separate faresto, from or inany part of the prescribed

of the months ofApril, May and June in each year as

so fixed .

have power to make such order thereon as itthinksfit,

and the applicant. An ordermade by the said Ministry
under this sub-sectionshallbe finaland not subjectto
appeal to any court,and may ,on the applicationeither
of the said Ministry or of the applicantfor the licence,
be enforceable(withoutprejudiceto any otherremedy)

CHAPTER 8 . 2
An Act for simplifying the preparation and
authentication of Commissions of the Peace , for
prescribingthe fees to be paid by Justices of
the Peace in respectof theirappointments , and
forother purposes connected therewith.
BE
[29th May ,1924.]
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-( 1) All commissions of the peace shall be
printedon parchmentwithblankstobefilledup inwrit-
ing or in print,and shallbe in the forms containedin the
First Schedule to this Act .
(2) A new commission in one of the forms contained
in the FirstSchedule to thisAct shall,as soon as may be
after the passing of thisAct ,be issuedto the keeper of
the rollsof every county and to the chiefofficerof every
corporationhaving a commission of the peace.
Every such new commission shall,as from the date
on which it is issued, supersede allcommissions of the
peace issuedbeforethat date for the county or borough
to which the new commission relates.
(3) The names of the justicesin each commission
shall be placed in a schedule annexed thereto,and the
Clerk of the Crown for Northern Ireland shall from time
to time, as occasionrequires,add in such schedule the
names of justicesappointed afterthe issueof such com-
mission , and delete from such schedule the names of
justiceswho have died and persons who have ceased to
hold the officeof justice.
(4) A recordshallbe kept at the officeof the Clerk
of the Crown for Northern Ireland of alljusticesof the
peace appointedunder any commission of the peace
hereafterissuedinthename ofHis Majesty.
(5) The Clerk of the Crown for Northern Ireland
shall issueto every justiceof the peace hereafterap-
pointed a certificatesignedby him in the form contained

CHAPTER 10 ,
An Act toamend the Public Libraries(Ireland)Acts, A.D.1924.
1855 to 1920 , in their applicationto Northern
Ireland,and forotherpurposesincidentalthereto.
[29th May ,1924.]
B E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthe same ,as follows:-
1.-(1)The councilof a countyshallhavepower,
by resolutionspecifyingthe area to which the resolution
extends, to adopt the Public Libraries(Ireland) Acts,
1855 to 1920 (in thisAct referredto as " the Public
LibrariesActs ")forallorany oftheruraldistrictssituate
in their county, and thereupon the provisionsof the
Public LibrariesActs , other than sections one and two
of the Public Libraries(Ireland)Act,1894,shall,subject
to the provisionsof thisAct ,apply with the necessary
modificationsas if the county councilwere the library
authorityforthepurpose of the exerciseand performance
of powers and dutiesunder the Public LibrariesActs for
the area specifiedin the resolution, to the exclusionof
the councilof any ruraldistricttherein.
(2) The powers of any ruraldistrictcouncilto adopt
or carry into execution the Public LibrariesActs shall
cease;and ,where any ruraldistrictcouncilwas ,immedi-
atelybeforethe passingof thisAct ,carryingthe Public
LibrariesActs intoexecution,the councilofthe county in
which the rural district is situate shall be deemed to have
adopted the Public LibrariesActs for that districtand
shallcarrythoseActs intoexecutionaccordingly.
(3) For the purpose of carryingthe Public Libraries
Acts into execution a county council shallappoint a
county library committee constituted in accordance
with the provisionscontained in the Schedule to this
Act ;but the actsof the county librarycommittee shall
be submittedto the county councilfortheirapproval.

SCHEDULE .
Constitutionof county librarycommittee.
The county librarycommittee shallconsistof the followingper-
(a) The chairman and vice-chairman of the county council;
(b) Three members ofthecouncil(ofwhom the chairman shallbe
one) of each ruraldistrict, as respectswhich the county
councilarecarryingthePublicLibrariesActs intoexecution;
(c) One member of the councilof each urban districtand one
commissioner of each town the council or commissioners of
which have relinquishedtheirpowers and duties under the
PublicLibrariesActs in favour of the county council;
(d ) An additionalnumber of members of the county council
equalto the number of ruraland urban districtsand towns
as respectswhich the county councilarecarryingthe Public
Libraries Acts into execution .
The county librarycommittee may choose in additionto the
aforesaidmembers furthermembers (notbeingmembers of any local
authorityin the county),not exceedinginnumber one for each rural
and urban districtand town as respectswhich the county councilis
carryingthe PublicLibrariesActs intoexecution.

CHAPTER 11 .
An Act to make provision for the temporary
exercise of the powers of Ministers of Northern
Ireland . [29th May , 1924.]
B E itenactedby theKing'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1. The Governor ofNorthern Irelandmay ,ifat any
time a Ministerof Northern Ireland is unable to act,
designateany ParliamentarySecretaryof the Ministry
orDepartment ofwhich such Ministeristhe head ,or any
other Minister of Northern Ireland, to act for such first-
mentioned Ministerduring such period, and subjectto
such conditions,as the saidGovernor may think fit;and ,
during the said period, and subject as aforesaid,
referencesin any enactment to such first-mentioned
Minister shall be construed as references to the Parlia-
mentary Secretaryor Ministerso designatedto act.

thousand,two hundred and two pounds .
2.-(1) The Ministry of Finance may borrow from
any person, by the issue of Treasury Bills or other-
wise,on the creditof the saidsum ,any sum or sums not
exceedinginthe whole threemillionpounds .
(2) The date ofpayment ofany Treasury Billsissued
under this section shall be a date not later than the
thirty-firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-
five .

sury Billsshallbe repaid,with any interestdue thereon,
out ofthe growing produce ofthe saidConsolidatedFund

Consolidated Fund and be availablein any manner in
which such Fund is available .

be deemed to have been appropriatedas from the date
of the passing of the Acts mentioned in the said Schedule
(A ),forthe severalservicesand purposesexpressedin
Schedule (B ) ofthisAct .

CHAPTER 15 .
An Act to make provision for the licensing of
wholesale dealers in eggs, the registrationof
premises where eggs are preserved, the better
testing, grading and packing of eggs, and the
better prevention of the sale of eggs unfit for
human food; and for other purposes connected
therewith. [29th May ,1924.]
B E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-

## Page 53

114 & 15 GEO .5.] Marketing ofEggs Act 47[Ch .15.]
(NorthernIreland),1924.
1.- (1)The MinistryofAgricultureforNorthern Ire-
land (in thisAct referredto as " the Ministry") shall
grant a licenceto carry on businessin Northern Ireland
as a wholesaledealerin eggs to any person applying for
such licencewho complies or undertakesto comply with
such conditionsinrelationto the preparationforsaleand
the consignmentof eggsasmay be prescribedfrom time
totime by theMinistry,withrespecttoany classofsuch
business, in order to secure-
(a) the proper testing,gradingand packing of such
eggs,and theirfreshnessand fitnessforthe food
of man ; and
(b) compliance with the requirements of thisAct
relatingto any such eggs.
For the purposes of thisAct the expression“ whole-
saledealer" includesany person who carrieson the busi-
nessofpurchasingeggsforre-saleotherwisethan by retail.
(2) Any person who carrieson businessin Northern
Ireland as a wholesale dealer in eggs without being
licensedforthe purpose under thissection,and any per-
son who dealsby way of wholesalepurchase of eggswith
any wholesale dealer who is not so licensed, shallbe
guiltyof an offenceagainst this Act ;
Provided that a person who dealswith a wholesale
dealerin eggswho isnot licensedas aforesaidshallnot be
liableto convictionunder thissub-section,ifhe provesto
the satisfactionofthe court before whom he ischarged that
he did not know ,and couldnot reasonablyhave known ,
that such wholesale dealer was not so licensed .
(3)A licencegranted under thissectionshallremain
in forceuntilsuspended or revoked by the Ministryby
reason of the non -compliance of the holder of the licence
with the conditionsprescribedas aforesaid, or for any
other sufficientreason;and a feeoftwenty shillingsshall
be paid tothe Ministryinrespectofthegrantofeach such
licence. A certifiedcopy of a licencemay be issuedupon
payment of a feeoftwo shillingsand sixpence.
(4)Ifany personforgesor fraudulentlyaltersoruses,
or permits to be fraudulentlyalteredor used,any licence
or certifiedcopy of a licenceissuedunder thissection,he
shallbe guiltyofan offenceagainstthisAct.

CHAPTER 20 .
An Act to amend , and remove doubts as to
certain provisionsof the Assurance Companies
Act , 1909 , as they apply in Northern Ireland.
[7th November ,1924.]
BEE itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of Northern
Irelandin thispresentParliamentassembled, and by
the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) Where an assurance company carrying on
or proposingto carryon any classof assurancebusiness
in Northern Ireland furnishesproof to the satisfaction
of the Ministry of Commerce for Northern Ireland (in
thisAct referredto as " the Ministry")that the company
has sincetheappointedday made ,orafterthepassingof
thisAct makes ,a depositin Great Britainin respectof
that class of assurance business in accordance with the
Assurance Companies Act ,1909 (in thisAct referredto as
" theAct of1909"),thenthecompany shall,solongasit
maintains such deposit, be exempt from making in
Northern Irelandin respectof the same classof business
any separatedepositwhich would ,apart from the provis-
ions of thissub-section, be requiredto be made by the
company under the Act of 1909 as itappliesin Northern
Ireland .
(2) Itishereby declaredthat,notwithstandingany
provisionscontained in Article12 of the Government of
Ireland(Companies,Societies,& c.) Order,1922,and any
Order of His Majesty in Council amending that Order
(whether made beforeor afterthe passingof thisAct), an
assurance company is not,and never has been,exempt
by reasononlyofsuch provisionsfrom making a deposit
in Northern Ireland in respect of any class of assur-ance business if, being a registered company , its
registeredoffice, or, not beinga registeredcompany ,
itshead office, was situateat the appointed day in any
part of Irelandotherthan Northern Ireland.
(3) In thissectionthe expression" the appointed
day " means the firstday of January ,nineteenhundred
and twenty -two .

with the Board of Trade and with the Ministryaccounts,

itshallbe a sufficientcompliance on the part of the com-

FOURTH SCHEDULE .
RULES FOR VALUING POLICIES .
1. The value of the policyis to be the differencebetween the
presentvalueofthe reversionin the sum assuredaccordingto the con-
tingencyupon which itispayable,includingany bonus added thereto,
and the present value of the future net premiums .
2. The net premium isto be such premium as accordingto the
assumed rateofinterestand rateof mortalityand the age ofthe person
whose lifeis assuredat his birthday next followingthe date of the
policyissufficientto provideforthe riskincurredby the company or
societyinissuingthepolicy,exclusiveofany additiontheretoforoffice
expenses and other charges :
Provided that-
(a) In the caseofa policyotherthan a policyforthe whole term
of lifeissuedbeforethe personwhose lifeisassuredattained
the age of ten years,the date of the policymay be assumed
to be one year afterthe actualdate,and,ifitisso assumed ,
the term of the policymay be assumed to be one year less
than the actual term :
(b) In the caseofa policyforthe whole term oflifeissuedbefore
the personwhose lifeisassuredattainedthe age often years,
no accountshallbe takenofany periodforwhichthepolicy
was inforcebeforethe anniversaryof thedate ofthe issueof
thepolicynext precedingthedate on which the age ofeleven
years was attained :
(c) In the case of a substitutedpolicy,the net premium shall
be calculatedwith referenceto such sum as, according to
the practiceof the societyor company for the time being,
would have been assuredby the premiums payableifthe
person upon whose lifethe substitutedpolicyisissuedhad
not been assured with the societyor company beforethe
issueofthatpolicy.
RULE FOR ASCERTAINING THE AMOUNT OF A FREE
PAID -UP POLICY .
The amount of a freepaid-up policyisto be a sum bearing the
same proportionto seventy-fiveper cent.of the valueof the policyas
thesum ofone pound bearstothe valueofthereversionin the sum of
one pound accordingto the contingencyupon which the sum assured
under the originalpolicywas payable.
GENERAL RULES APPLICABLE BOTH FOR VALUING
POLICIES AND FOR ASCERTAINING THE AMOUNT OF A FREE
PAID -UP POLICY .
1. Interestisto be assumed at the rateof four per centum per
annum .

## Page 113

[14 & 15 GEO .5.] IndustrialAssurance 107[Ch .21.]
Act (Northern Ireland), 1924.
2. The rate of mortalityisto be assumed accordingto the table A.D. 1924.
containedin the Sixth column of Table G in the Supplement to the
Sixty-fifthAnnual Report of the Registrar-Generalof Births,Deaths
and MarriagesinEngland and Wales - Part I.
3,The age ofthepersonwhose lifeisassuredshallbe obtained
by adding to the age attainedby him at his birthday next afterthe
date of the issueof the policy,the durationof the policyin completed
yearsatthedateasatwhich thevalueofthepolicyisrequiredto be
ascertained .
4. In the caseof a policyissuedfora term otherthan the whole
term of life,the remainingterm at the date at which the valueofthe
policyisrequiredto be ascertainedshallbe obtainedby deductingfrom
the originalterm of the policythe durationof the policyin completed
years at thatdate.

CHAPTER 23 .
An Act to continue certain Expiring Laws as
respects Northern Ireland .
[7th November , 1924].
WHEREASTHEREAStheActs(whetherpassedbytheParlia-
ment of the United Kingdom or by the
Parliament of Northern Ireland) mentioned in the
Scheduleto thisAct are,insofarasthey areinforcein
Northern Ireland and are temporary in theirduration,
limited to expire on the severaldates specifiedin the
several Parts of the said Schedule in connection with such
Acts respectively:
And whereas itisexpedientto provideforthe continuance
as in thisAct mentioned of those Acts , and of the enact-
ments amending or affectingthe same :
Be it thereforeenacted by the King's most Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthe same ,asfollows:-
A.D. 1924
Continuance
of Acts in1.-(1) The Acts mentioned in the severalParts of
the Schedule to thisAct shall,to the extent specifiedin Schedule.
column three of that Schedule, be continued as respects
Northern Irelanduntilthe thirty-firstday of December ,
nineteenhundred and twenty -five, and shallthen expire
unless further continued .
(2) Any unrepealed enactments amending or affect-
ing the enactments continued by thisAct shall,in so far
as they are temporary in theirduration,be continued in
likemanner ,whether they are mentioned in the Schedule
to this Act or not .
and2.-(1) This Act may be citedas the Expiring Laws Shorttitle
Continuance Act (Northern Ireland),1924.
(2) Referencesin thisAct to any enactments of the
Parliament of the United Kingdom shallbe construedas
referencesto thoseenactments as they apply inNorthern
Ireland .
(3) Nothing inthisAct shallbe construedas affect-
ingany enactment in so faras the enactment relatesto a
matter with respectto which the Parliament of Northern
Irelandhas not power to make laws.

CHAPTER 24 .
An Act to make provision for the permanent
adoption in Northern Ireland of the Time
adopted for use in Great Britain.
[7th November ,1924.]
Whereas it is expedient that provisionshould be
made that the time for generalpurposes in Northern
Ireland should at all times be the same as the time for
generalpurposesin Great Britain:
Be itthereforeenactedby theKing'smost Excellent
Majesty,and the Senateand theHouse of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1. Any enactment ofthe Parliament ofthe United
Kingdom or Order of His Majestyin Councilpassedor
made afterthe passingofthisAct and forthe time being
in force, which makes or continuesany provisionswith
respectto the time forgeneralpurposesin Great Britain,
shallapply,with respectto the time forgeneralpurposes
in Northern Ireland, tothe extentto which itapplies

## Page 121

[14 & 15 GEO . 5.1 115Time Act [Ch . 24,25.]
(Northern Ireland), 1924.
inGreat Britain,and duringthesame periodsinany year, A.D.1924.
and subjectto the same limitations,as may be forthe
time being in forcefor or with respectto the adoption
of such time in Great Britain; and the Time (Ireland)
Act ,1916,shall,as respectsNorthern Ireland,have effect
accordingly.
2. ThisAct may be citedastheTime Act (Northern
Ireland), 1924, and shallbe construed as one with the
Time (Ireland)Act,1916,asthatAct appliesinNorthern
Ireland,and thatAct and thisAct may be citedtogether
as the Time Acts (Northern Ireland),1916 and 1924.
6 & 7 Geo . 5 ,
с .45 .

andconstruc-tion .

SCHEDULES .
FIRST SCHEDULE .
PART I.
SUPPLEMENTAL PROVISIONS RELATING TO RIGHT TO UNEMPLOYMENT
BENEFIT .
1. Benefitshallbe payable in respectof each week afterthe first
threedays of a continuousperiodof unemployment .
2. No personshallreceivebenefitin respectof any periodof less
than one day .
3. The followingprovisionsshallhave effectfor the purpose of
determiningthenumber ofcontributionswhich aretobe takenasstanding
at any time to the creditof any person :-
(a) Where owing to the factthatthe wages or otherremuneration
ofan employed personarepaidatintervalsgreaterthan a week ,
or forany otherlikereason,contributionsare paid in respect
ofany personatintervalsgreaterthan a week ,thatpersonshall
be entitledto treateach of thosecontributionsas being such
number of contributionsas thereare weeks in the period in
respectof which the contributionwas paid;
(b) There shallbe deducted from the aggregatenumber of contri-
butionsactuallypaid in respectof him one contributionin
respectof each day of benefitpreviouslyreceivedby him ,
exclusiveof any benefitreceivedin respectof the periodbe-
tween the seventh day of November , nineteenhundred and
twenty,and the terminationofthe fourthspecialperiod,or in
the caseof benefitreceivedin respectof the periodbeforethe
eighthday of November ,nineteenhundred and twenty, five
contributionsinrespectofeach week ofbenefitreceived.
4. Any time duringwhich a personisunder the provisionsof the
principalAct disqualified,otherwisethanby reasonofbeinginreceipt
of sickness or disablement benefit or disablement allowance under the
enactmentsrelatingto NationalHealth Insurance,forreceivingbenefit
shallbe excludedinthecomputationofcontinuousperiodsofunemploy-
ment under this Part of this Schedule .
5. A periodof unemployment shallnot be deemed to commence
untilthe date on which the insuredcontributormakes applicationfor
benefitin the prescribedmanner :
Provided that regulationsmay be made under sectionthirty-five
of the principalAct forauthorisingsome earlierdate to be substituted
forthe date ofthe applicationin casesin which good causeisshown for
delay inmaking the application.

Act (Northern Ireland), 1924 .
CHAPTER 26 .
An Act to apply a Sum out of the Consolidated
Fund of Northern Ireland to the service of the
year ending on the thirty-firstday of March ,
nineteenhundred and twenty -five,and to appro-
priate the further Supplies granted in this
Session of Parliament . [7th November ,1924.]
BEE it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
forthe purpose of making good the supply and applying
the sums which the House of Commons have , in pur-
suance of recommendations from the Governor of Nor-
thern Ireland, granted to His Majesty in thisSession of
Parliament , as follows :-
GRANT OUT OF CONSOLIDATED FUND .
1. The MinistryofFinanceforNorthernIreland(inthisAct referredto as " the Ministryof Finance ") may
issue out of the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland,
and apply towards making good the supply granted to
His Majesty for the serviceof the year ending on the
thirty-firstday of March , nineteenhundred and twenty-
five,the sum ofthreehundred and ninetythousand,nine
hundred and sixty-threepounds .
2.-(1) The Ministryof Finance may borrow from
any person, by the issueof Treasury Billsor otherwise,
on the creditof the saidsum , any sum or sums not ex-
ceedingin the whole two hundred thousand pounds .
(2) Any money borrowedotherwisethanon Treasury
Billsshallbe repaid, with any interestdue thereon, out
of the growing produce of the saidConsolidatedFund at
any date not laterthan the quarter next succeedingto
that in which the money was borrowed.
(3) The date of payment of any Treasury Bills
issued under this section shall be a date not later than the
thirty-firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-
five .

An Act to make better provision in Northern
Ireland with regard to children of unmarried
parents ; and for other purposes connected
therewith . [7th November , 1924.]
B E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.- (1) Where a man isallegedby the mother to be
the father of her illegitimatechild, and has been sum-
moned in accordance with the provisionsof thisAct to
appear beforea courtofsummary jurisdiction,constituted
as hereinafterprovided actingforthe petty sessionsdis-
trictor placeinwhich the mother resides,or inwhich the
mother or her illegitimatechildisinreceiptofrelieffrom
the poor ratesofany poor law union,the courtshallhave
power to make an order (in thisAct referredto as an
AffiliationOrder ") adjudging the man to be the
putative fatherof the child. An AffiliationOrder may
provide , under such conditionsas the Court seesfit,for
the payment by such putative father of
66
(a) the expensesincidentalto the birthofthe child;
(b) ifthe childhas died beforethe making of the
AffiliationOrder the funeralexpenses of such
child,to an amount not exceedingfivepounds ;
and
(c) a weekly sum of money not exceeding twenty
shillingsin any one week in respect of the
maintenance and education of the child .
Any provisionin an AffiliationOrder for any such
payment shallcontinuein forceuntilthe child,to whom
it relates,shall,ifa male,attainthe age of fifteenyears
or if a female, attainthe age of sixteenyears or marry
under that age,and,except for the recovery of arrears
or funeralexpenses, for no longer period, but no such
provisionforthe payment of a weekly sum shallcontinue
in force after the death of such child.

CHAPTER 29 ,
An Act to prescribethe method ofascertainingthe
annual rateable value of certain houses and
buildingsinNorthern Irelandforthe purposes of
the Irish Valuation Acts .
BE it
[7th November ,1924.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1. (1) The Commissioner of Valuation shall,Vin
carrying out the annual revisionof the valuation of
rateable tenements and hereditaments , cause the net
annualvalueof any house or buildingto be estimated
(notwithstanding anything contained in sectioneleven
15&16Vict,,of the Valuation(Ireland) Act, 1852) by takingthe netc . 63 .
annual value of that house or buildingas contained in
the revisedvaluationlistsin forceforthe standard year,
and adding an amount equal to fifteenper cent.of such
last -mentioned net annual value :
Provided that-
(i) In thefollowingcasesthe net annual value shall
be estimated with reference to comparable
valuations as defined in this section, and
the net annual value so estimated shall then be
increasedby an amount equal to fifteenper
cent. thereof, namely-
(a) inany casewhere the house or buildingwas
or isto be valued forthe firsttime at any
date subsequent to the firstday of March ,
nineteen hundred and fourteen ;
(b) inany casewhere the valuationofthehouse
or building as set forth in the revised
valuationlistsinforceforthe standard year
was fixedat a date so long antecedent to the
standard year that it does not represent
the truerateablevalueforthat year ;
(c) in any case where thehouse orbuildinghas
been adapted for some purpose other than

## Page 155

[14 & 15 GEO .5.] ValuationActs Amendment [Ch . 29.] 149
Act (Northern Ireland), 1924.
that for which itwas fittedat the time when A.D.1924.
its net annual value was estimated for the
purpose of the valuation in force for the
standard year ;
(ii) In any case(not being a caseto which paragraph
(i) (b) of the provisoto thissub-sectionapplies)
where structural alterations or additions have
been made toa house orbuildingwhose valuation
was contained in the valuation listsin force for
the standardyear,but where such alterationsor
additions eitherhad not been carriedout ,or were
not taken into account ,at the time when those
listswere prepared,then the netannual value of
the house or buildingshallbe estimatedat the
amount at which the house or buildingwould
have been valued if those alterations or additions
had been thentakenintoaccount,togetherwithan
addition equal to fifteenper cent. of that
amount ;
(iii) The valuationof a house or buildingshallnot,
by reason of thisAct , be fixedat an amount
in excess of the amount of the valuation which
would , apart from thisAct ,have been made in
regardto that house or building.
(2) Nothing in thisAct shallaffectthe rightof any
person,county councilor urban districtcounciltotake or
continue,under the IrishValuationActs,any proceedings
by way of appeal againstor in respectof the valuation
of any tenement orhereditament made (whether before
or afterthe passingof thisAct)in the manner directed
by thisAct .
(3) In thissection-
The expression" house or building" includesany
rateable tenement or hereditament which would , apart
from this Act ,have been valued in the manner directed
by sectioneleven of the Valuation (Ireland) Act , 1852,
with respecttohouses and buildings,but does not include
any dwellinghouse to which the provisionsofparagraph
(f) insub-section(2) of sectioneighteenofthe Increaseof
Rent and Mortgage Interest(Restrictions) Act , 1920, Geo.5.c.17.
apply :
ود

months ended on the thirty-firstday ofMarch, nineteen
hundred and fifteen :

2.-(1) ThisAct may be citedas the Valuation Acts
Amendment Act (Northern Ireland), 1924, and shall be
construed as one with the IrishValuation Acts as they
apply in Northern Ireland.
(2) This Act shallhave effectasfrom the firstday of

CHAPTER iii.
An Act to confer further Powers on the Belfast
City and DistrictWater Commissioners .
[29th May , 1924.]
WHEREAS by the BelfastWater Acts 1840 to 1923 the
BelfastCityand DistrictWater Commissioners(herein-
aftercalled" the Commissioners") were incorporated
and by those Acts theirpowers were from time to time
regulated and extended .
And whereas itisexpedientto authorisethe Com-

of the transferor deposit of securitiesrepresenting
investments of the Commissioners ' Funds .
And whereas itisexpedient to authorisethe Com-

the Bathing Stationat the Antrim Road Works .

31 of the Belfast Water Act 1897 and Section 15 of the

And whereas the Commissioners are the owners of

effected without the authority of the Parliament of
Northern Ireland .

PART IV .- TRAMWAY .
32. Subjectto the provisionsofthisAct the Corpora-
tion may form lay down work use and maintain in the
linesand situationsand accordingto the levelsshown on
the depositedplans and sectionsand in allrespectsin
accordance with those plans and sectionsthe tramway
hereinafterdescribedwith allproper railsplatesworks
and conveniences connected therewith .
The Tramway hereinbeforereferredto and author-
isedby thisAct issituatewholly withinthe cityand isas
follows-
A Tramway (double line) 1 furlong2.65 chains or
thereaboutsin length commencing in CastleStreetby a
junction with the existingtramway therein near the
junction of Queen Street with Castle Street and terminat-
ing in Wellington Place by a junctionwith the existing
tramway thereinnear the saidjunctionof Queen Street
with Castle Street .
33. The Tramway shallbe constructedon a gauge of
four feeteightand a-halfinchesand carriagesor trucks
adapted to run on railwaysshallnot be used to run there-
on .
34. If the Tramway be not completed and opened
forpublictrafficwithinfiveyearsfrom the passingofthis
Act then on the expirationof that periodthe powers by
thisAct granted for constructingthe same or otherwise
inrelationtheretoshallceaseexcept as to so much of the
Tramway as shallthen be completed.
35. Subjectto the provisionsof thisAct the Tram-
way shallforallpurposesbe deemed to form part of the
UndertakingTramway Undertakingand oftheCorporationTramways .
Inspection
by Ministry
of Home
Affairs .
36. No part of the Tramway shallbe opened for
publictrafficuntilithas been inspectedand certifiedto
be fitforsuch trafficby an officerappointedby the Minis-
try of Home Affairs.

(Northern Ireland),1924.

PART V. OMNIBUSES .
42.-(1) Subject to the provisionsof thisAct the
Corporation may provide and maintain and may run
omnibuses withinthe city.
(2) The Corporation may purchase by agreement
take on leaseand hold landsand buildingsand may erect
on any lands acquired by them omnibus carriageand
motor houses buildingsand sheds and may provide such
plantappliancesand conveniencesas may be requisite
or expedientfor the establishmentrunning equipment
maintenance and repair of such omnibuses but the Cor-
porationshallnot createor permit any nuisanceon any
landsupon which they erectany such housesbuildings
or sheds .
(3) Every omnibus moved by electricalpower shall
be so equipped and worked as to prevent any interference
with telegraphiccommunication by means of any
telegraphsof the Post-Master General.
(4) The Corporationshallperform in respectof the
omnibuses provided under thisSection such servicesin
regard to the conveyance of mails as are prescribedby
the Conveyance of Mails Act 1893 in the case of a
Tramway towhich thatAct applies.
(5)In thisPart ofthisAct the expression" omnibus "
has the same meaning asisassignedto thatexpressionby
the Town Police Clauses Act 1889 .

Preamble .
CHAPTER v .
An Act to provide forthe Transfer to the Mayor
Aldermen and Burgesses of the City of London-
derry of the Undertaking of the Londonderry
Bridge Commissioners and to authorise the said
Mayor Aldermen and Burgesses to maintain
work and regulatethe same ; to widen raiseand
reconstruct the Londonderry Bridge and the
approaches thereto ; to construct works for the
purposes of their water undertaking and to
make a street improvement ; to confer further
powers upon the said Mayor Aldermen and
Burgesses with respecttotheirWater Electricity
Markets and Omnibus Undertakings ; to make
furtherprovisionforthe improvement and good
government of the City; and forother purposes.
[29th May , 1924.]
WHEREAS the City of Londonderry (in thisAct
called" the City ") isunder and by virtueof the Local
Government (Ireland) Act 1898 a county borough and is
subjectto the Acts relatingto municipalcorporationsin
Northern Irelandand theMayor Aldermen and Burgesses
oftheCityactingby the Councilthereof(inthisAct called
" theCorporation")aretheurban sanitaryauthorityfor
the districtthereofunder the Public Health (Ireland)
Acts :

(Northern Ireland), 1924 .

ofthelast-named Act constructedtheLondonderry Bridge

Bridge "): and the Honourable the IrishSociety con-

expedient that the costthereofshould be spread over a
term ofyears.
And whereas the Bridge and the Ferriesundertaking
of the Commissioners includepermanent works and itis
expedient thatthe repayment ofthe moneys to be paid by
the Corporationinrespectofthedebtsand liabilitiesofthe
Commissioners should be spread over a term ofyears.
And whereas the Corporationhave complied with
the requirements of the Borough Funds (Ireland) Act
1888 inrelationto the promotion ofthe BillforthisAct .
And whereas plans and sectionsshowing the lines
situationand levelsof the works authorisedby thisAct
and plans showing the lands which may be acquired or
used under the powers ofthisAct and a book ofreference
to those plans containingthe names of the owners or
reputed owners lesseesor reputed lesseesand of the
occupiersofand describingsuch landshave been deposited
with the Clerkofthe Crown and Peace forthe County of
Londonderry and ofthe County ofthe Cityand areinthis
Act referredto respectivelyas " the despositedplans
sections and book of reference ."

## Page 323

NOTE .
By the Government of IrelandAct ,1920 (10 & 11 Geo .5,c.67),
section6 (2),itisprovided that--
Where any Act of the Parliament of Northern Ireland deals with any
matter with respectto which that Parliament has power to make laws which
isdealt with by any Act of the Parliament of the United Kingdom passed
after the appointed day * and extending to the part of Ireland within its
jurisdictionthe Act of the Parliament of Northern Ireland shall be read
subject to the Act of the Parliament of the United Kingdom and so far as
itisrepugnant to that Act , but no further,shallbe void.
and section(3)providesthat-
Any order rule or regulationmade in pursuance of or having the force
of an Act of Parliament of the United Kingdom shallbe deemed to be a
provision of an Act within the meaning of this section.
*3rd May , 1921 .
